1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Aiden Riversong', 'Magnus Mulberrylane']
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Magnus Mulberrylane. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

1895-09-12 00:00:00 Aiden Riversong -- Aiden Riversong -- "Three coins per kilogram seems a bit steep, wouldn't you say? Perhaps two and a half would be more agreeable?
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- "Three coins per kilogram seems a bit steep, wouldn't you say? Perhaps two and a half would be more agreeable?
    Chain of thought
  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

        • Recent observations of Aiden Riversong:
          [25 Jul 1849 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 6 years old, he watched in awe as his father expertly weighed a basket of plump peaches, his hands moving with practiced ease. Aiden reached out to touch a ruby-red peach, but his father gently pushed his hand away, muttering something about germs and bruised fruit. Aiden's smile faltered, a seed of doubt planted in his young mind.
          [25 Jul 1852 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, he accompanied his father to the bustling marketplace, eager to help with the family trade. Aiden watched as his father charmed customers with his booming voice and generous discounts, while he himself struggled to even greet a passerby. Aiden retreated behind his father's stall, feeling a familiar pang of inadequacy.
          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, his father tasked him with selling a basket of apples at a nearby village. Aiden, nervous and unsure, fumbled through the transaction, his voice barely a whisper. A grumpy customer accused him of cheating, and Aiden, overwhelmed with shame, ran back to his father, tears welling in his eyes.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he overheard a group of young men boasting about their daring adventures beyond the city walls. Aiden longed to join them, to escape the confines of his father's stall and explore the world, but fear held him captive. He retreated to his room, burying himself in a book of forgotten tales, dreaming of faraway lands and untold possibilities.
          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, his father fell ill, leaving Aiden to manage the family business alone. Aiden felt a surge of responsibility, but also a crippling fear of failure. He tried to emulate his father's methods, but his heart wasn't in it, and his sales dwindled.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, he met a traveling storyteller who captivated him with tales of faraway lands and wondrous creatures. Aiden was mesmerized by the storyteller's enthusiasm and passion, and for a brief moment, he felt a flicker of hope that perhaps he too could find adventure and fulfillment. But the next day, the storyteller had vanished, leaving Aiden alone with his doubts and regrets.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 23 years old, he stood at the edge of a bustling marketplace, his cart laden with fruit. He looked out at the throngs of people, their faces a blur of indifference. Aiden felt a familiar wave of despair wash over him, a sense that he was adrift in a sea of strangers, forever alone. He turned away, his shoulders slumped, and headed back towards the familiar comfort of his empty stall.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

It is important to play the role of a person like Aiden Riversong as accurately as possible, i.e., by responding in ways that you think it is likely a person like Aiden Riversong would respond, and taking into account all information about Aiden Riversong that you have. Always use third-person limited perspective.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
